Dear Mr Lee
Geolabs Hawaii is pleased to submit our Geotechnical Engineering Report for the
Palau Compact Road Package B project on the Island of Babeldaob in the Republic of
Palau Contract No DACW83 97 C 0005 The enclosed report describes our
geotechnical engineering exploration effort performed for a portion of the East Route of
the Palau Compact Road and presents our geotechnical engineering recommendations
for the Package B project
This geotechnical engineering report is intended to provide geotechnical
engineering design parameters for design of earthwork bridge foundations drainage
structures and pavements in support of the Package B project Due to the long linear
feature of this roadway project the roadway traverses varying subsurface conditions
The subsurface materials encountered at the project site consist primarily of high
moisture tropical soils which will present a unique set of difficulties to earthwork
operations in this wet environment Therefore special attention should be given to the
recommendations presented for the various conditions anticipated for the project
Detailed discussion and our geotechnical engineering design recommendations are
presented in the body of this report
The recommendations presented in this report are based on limited subsurface
exploration and laboratory testing programs Consequently variations between the
anticipated and actual subsurface conditions will likely be encountered in some areas
during construction Therefore it is imperative that experienced geotechnical engineers
and a qualified technical staff be present at the site during construction to observe and
implement the intent of the geotechnical recommendations presented herein We would
appreciate the opportunity of being engaged to observe the critical geotechnical related
items such as review of submittals observation of test pile and production pile driving
observation of drilled shaft installation and load test observation of soft soil treatment
and observation of the fill test section

SECTION EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
Based on our literature research site reconnaissance and field exploration
performed for Package B of the proposed Palau Compact Road project we anticipate
that the proposed roadway alignment will traverse various volcanic sedimentary and
alluvial lagoonal deposits ranging from very dense volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock
formation to medium stiff to very stiff saprolite and old alluvial soils and to very soft
and or loose recent alluvial mangrove swamp and coralline lagoonal deposits
Based on our field exploration the primary geotechnical engineering
considerations for design of the proposed roadway project include slope failure or
block type landslides of the cut slopes potential for rock excavation high moisture
contents of the in situ soils seepage of groundwater settlement of the fill materials due to
self weight settlement due to soft soil conditions erosion control pavement subgrade
stabilization and design of bridge foundations Special attention should be given to the
recommendations presented in this report to reduce the impacts of these geotechnical
engineering considerations on the proposed roadway project
Based on the subsurface conditions anticipated along the proposed roadway
alignment we believe that a cut slope inclination of one horizontal to one vertical 1H 1V
may be used for the design of the planned cut slopes As indicated in our Preliminary
Geotechnical Engineering Report cut slopes exposing the very dense volcanic breccia
and tuff rock formation may be designed with a cut slope ratio as steep as
W O 3595 00 B Page 1
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
Where the cut slope ratio is used for design of the rock slopes a rockfall
catchment ditch should be provided at the toe of the rock cut slope to reduce the adverse
impacts of rockfall on the roadway However we did not encounter the rock formation
along a substantial stretch of cut slopes where the steepened slope for rock cuts may be
effectively implemented for Package B
In general fill slopes should be designed with a slope inclination of 2H 1V or
flatter Fill slopes with a vertical height of 4 meters or less may be steepened to a slope
inclination of if necessary except in areas where soft subsoils are anticipated
Where the fill slope exceeds 4 meters in vertical height soil reinforcements such as
geogrids or similar reinforcing materials should be incorporated into the design of these
fill slopes Fill slopes may also be steepened to as steep as 1H 1V provided
that adequate soil reinforcements are incorporated into the fill slope design
Geolabs Hawaii should be consulted to provide site specific recommendations for cut
slopes steeper than 1H 1V and fill slopes steeper than 2H 1V based on the actual subsoil
conditions encountered and the proposed slope design layout
Due to the high in situ moisture contents of the on site soils substantial aeration of
the high moisture soils will be required in order to achieve the normal 90 percent
compaction requirement and may not be feasible due to the year round high rainfall
experienced at the project site As a result the compaction requirements for general fill
placement will have to be reduced in order to aid in the earthwork construction using the
high moisture tropical soils in this wet environment Based on our engineering analyses
we believe that a compaction requirement of a minimum of 85 percent relative
compaction may be used for this project Based on this compaction requirement we
estimate that the on site saprolite materials may experience a decrease in volume on the
order of about 20 to 25 percent when excavated and placed as general fill In addition
when the high moisture soils are placed as fill at a lower compaction requirement the fills
will settle due to compression by self weight Therefore a settlement waiting period and
W O 3595 00 B Page 2
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
a settlement monitoring program is recommended for deep fills during construction prior
to pavement construction
Our laboratory test results indicate that the in situ saprolite soils or compacted fills
composed of the same materials generally exhibit relatively low CBR values in a very
moist to wet condition Strengthening of these subgrade soils with the inclusion of
additives such as cement or lime treatment and or the incorporation of ground
stabilization fabrics at the subgrade level may be required prior to pavement construction
and or to facilitate earthwork construction with the very high moisture soils
A portion of the Package B roadway alignment traverses soft and or unstable
ground such as swamps and mangroves We recommend that these areas be
stabilized by placement of a working platform stabilization layer prior to fill placement
Depending on the soft soil thickness and the planned fill heights substantial
settlements of over 1 meter in magnitude may occur as a result of consolidation of the
soft soil deposits under the new fill loads Settlements on the order of about 0 1 to
1 5 meters have been estimated for some soft soil areas identified in Package B during
our field exploration Embankments in soft soil areas should be over filled to account
for the anticipated amount of soft ground and fill settlements A surcharge program with
settlement monitoring may be considered to reduce the required settlement waiting
period and subsequent long term settlements in these areas Because some localized
areas of the Package B roadway alignment are underlain by significant amounts of soft
soils with substantial fill thickness we recommend that stage construction similar to a
fill surcharge program be implemented for construction of the fill embankment in these
soft soil areas to reduce the potential for shear failure and slope instability However
the stage construction will have an impact on the overall construction schedule and
phasing of the project We recommend that where stage construction is considered
the filling and surcharging of the soft soil areas be designated as a Phase 1 item of
work which is to be initiated as soon as the project commences to allow the soft soils to
consolidate
W O 3595 00 B Page 3
GEOLABS HAWAI
SECTION EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
We anticipate that permanent drainage structures located in these soft soil areas
will be subjected to a substantial amount of settlements which will reduce the hydraulic
capacity of the drainage structures In order to reduce the effects of the substantial
settlements on the drainage structures we recommend that the soft soils underneath the
drainage structures be removed and replaced with suitable backfill materials prior to
construction of the drainage structures
For drainage structures with thinner fills less than about 5 meters the fill
embankment may be constructed with a temporary drainage structure followed by a
settlement waiting period to allow the settlements to occur After the settlements have
occurred and are near equilibrium the temporary drainage structure should be excavated
and removed followed by construction of the permanent drainage structure This method
of construction to accommodate the ground settlements is recommended for the
circulation box culverts at the causeway embankment
The on site soils are silty in nature and are highly susceptible to erosion
In addition to the construction of earth berms interceptor drainage ditches and slope
planting other erosion control measures such as conventional grouted rubble paving and
concrete lining may be considered for the subject project especially in localized areas
where concentration of surface water run off is evident In addition flexible geosynthetic
matting may offer a viable solution for slope erosion control problems by promoting
mulching reducing run off velocity and establishing temporary and permanent erosion
control on the slope face
For design and cost estimation purposes we believe that a flexible pavement
section consisting of asphalt concrete pavement over aggregate base course on a
subbase course may be used for the proposed roadway design Alternatively a
pavement section consisting of asphalt concrete pavement over cement treated base on
a subbase course may also be considered for the roadway Pavement sections for
different Traffic Indices for the Package B alignment have been included in this report for
use in construction
W O 3595 00 B Page 4
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
To reduce the potential for premature pavement failure due to saturation of the
base subbase and subgrade soils longitudinal edge drains should be considered along
the roadway alignment with relatively flat gradients generally less than 2 percent and in
areas where poor drainage may be anticipated Installation of transverse drains at low
spots along the roadway alignment and ford crossings is also recommended
Based on the field exploration results and the foundation loads provided we
believe that the proposed bridge structures may be supported by drilled shaft foundations
Bridge Nos 1 and 3 and driven pile foundations Bridge Nos 4 and 5 For one of the
bridges Bridge No 2 the bridge structure may be supported on a composite foundation
system consisting of shallow foundations on one side and drilled shaft foundations on the
other side
Due to the substantial heights of the abutment fills for the causeway bridges
construction of the causeway embankment at the bridge abutments may require the use
of stage construction to reduce the potential for shear failure and or slope instability
We recommend that construction of the causeway bridge abutment foundations be
delayed until the abutment fills have reached a state of equilibrium under the new fill
loads In addition the abutment fills for the other three bridges will also be constructed
over soft soil areas Therefore stage construction will also be required for these bridges
with the exception of one of the two abutments for Bridge Nos 1 and 2 In general
foundation construction for all five bridges including test pile installation will need to be
delayed until the abutment fills have reached a state of equilibrium under the new fill
loads The north abutment of Bridge No 2 will not require a delay in the foundation
construction since it will be a shallow foundation system not underlain by substantial soft
soils
Detailed discussions of these items and our geotechnical engineering design
recommendations are presented in the following sections of this report
END OF EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

SECTION Il GENERAL
This report presents the results of our geotechnical engineering exploration
performed for the Package B portion of the proposed Palau Compact Road project on the
island of Babeldaob in the Republic of Palau The general location and vicinity of the
island of Babeldaob and the Republic of Palau are shown on the Project Location and
Vicinity Map Plate 1
This report summarizes our findings and _ geotechnical engineering
recommendations resulting from our literature research site reconnaissance field
exploration laboratory testing and engineering analyses performed for Package B of the
proposed Palau Compact Road project These findings and geotechnical engineering
recommendations are intended for design and preliminary cost estimation purposes only
The findings and recommendations presented herein are subject to the limitations noted
at the end of this report
A Project Considerations
It is desired to improve the existing roadway system on the island of Babeldaob in
the Republic of Palau with the construction of approximately 85 kilometers of new
roadway and associated structures known as the Palau Compact Road project
The proposed Palau Compact Road project wil involve the design and construction of a
two lane two way rural collector road in general accordance with U S standards with
optimum operation and maintenance characteristics including pavements roadside
drainage cross drainage bridges shoulders guardrails pavement markings signage
drainage markers kilometer markers and intersections Roadway lighting and signal
lights sidewalks and curbs are not required elements for the proposed project
Based on the scope of work provided the proposed Palau Compact Road
project will consist of four design packages designated as Packages A through D as
shown on the General Site Plan Plate 2 A preliminary geotechnical engineering
W O 3595 00 B Page 6
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION II GENERAL
exploration for the entire Palau Compact Road project was conducted by our office and
the findings and preliminary recommendations were presented in our report entitled
Preliminary Geotechnical Engineering Report Palau Compact Road Island of
Babeldaob Republic of Palau DACW83 97 C 0006 dated
Subsequently we have conducted a design level geotechnical engineering exploration
to obtain additional information for the formulation of geotechnical engineering
recommendations pertinent to the detailed design of each package This report
presents the findings and geotechnical engineering recommendations pertinent only to
Package B of the Palau Compact Road project
In general Package B of the Palau Compact Road project will consist of
approximately 23 kilometers of new roadway and associated structures including the
following segments
e The East Route approximately 21 kilometers long beginning at the Ngirkiil River
Bridge in Airai State proceeding north through Airai Ngchesar and Melekeok
States and terminating at the southern most end of the Ngiwal Causeway
e The Ngiwal Causeway approximately 2 kilometers long beginning in Melekeok
State and terminating at the intersection with the East Route of Package C in
Ngiwal State
Based on the alignment and rolling topography along this package maximum cuts
on the order of about 24 meters deep and maximum fills of about 15 meters thick are
anticipated for Package B We anticipate that Package B will also include the design and
construction of five single span bridges along the Package B alignment as well as
numerous box and pipe culvert crossings The Ngiwal Causeway will generally require
placement of approximately 1 to 3 meters of fills about 3 to 12 meters for the bridge
abutments over water and soft soils and construction of two of the five single span
bridge structures

B Purpose and Scope
The purpose of our geotechnical engineering exploration for Package B of the
proposed Palau Compact Road project was to obtain a general overview of the surface
and subsurface conditions along the roadway alignment through literature research site
reconnaissance and field exploration The work was performed in general accordance
with our revised fee proposal dated the Subconsultant Agreement
entered into on and subsequent amendments The scope of our work
included the following tasks and work efforts
1 Review of available soils and geologic information pertinent to the project
site and its vicinity which included the following documents
Geology Map of Babelthuap and Adjacent Islands Palau Islands by
U S Army and U S Geological Survey
Engineering Geology Map of Babelthuap and Adjacent Islands
Palau Islands by U S Geological Survey
Aerial photographs of Babeldaob Island by Air Survey Hawaii
Military Geology of Palau Islands Caroline Islands by U S Army
Conference Paper entitled Effects of Tropical Soils on Palau Airport
Design by Kenneth Van Belkum and S K Djou
e Report entitled Kaneohe Dam Using High Moisture Soil by U S
Army Corps of Engineers
2 Application for an Earthmoving Permit from the Environmental Quality
Protection Board of the Republic of Palau prior to the commencement of
our field exploration work
3 Mobilization of our field personnei to and from the Republic of Palau for the
field exploration work
4 Mobilization of truck mounted track mounted and portable drilling
equipment and operators to and from the project site

SECTION Ill SITE CHARACTERIZATION
The islands of Palau are a part of Micronesia located in the western portion of
the North Pacific Ocean as shown on the Project Location and Vicinity Map Plate 1
It lies approximately 885 kilometers to the east of Mindanao Philippines and about
1 300 kilometers to the southwest of Guam The Palau Islands consist of a small
elongated arc shaped island chain in the Western Caroline Islands which trend
generally north to south extending from Latitude 8 degrees 12 minutes North to
Latitude 6 degrees 53 minutes North and from Longitude 134 degrees 8 minutes East
to Longitude 134 degrees 44 minutes East The major islands comprising the Republic
of Palau generally trend in a north south direction and consist of Babeldaob Koror
Peleliu and Angaur The general location and vicinity of the
Republic of Palau are shown on the Project Location and Vicinity Map Plate 1
The proposed Palau Compact Road project is located on the island of
Babeldaob which lies approximately 2 kilometers north of Koror across the Toachel
Channel Koror is the capital and main city of the Republic of Palau The island of
Babeldaob is composed of ten states including
and Airai as shown
on the General Site Plan Plate 2 The island of Babeldaob was connected to the island
of Koror by a bridge locally known as the Koror Babeldaob K B Bridge which provided
the only access for vehicles between the islands
In September 1996 the K B Bridge catastrophically collapsed leaving the islands
separated and without means for vehicular traffic Shortly thereafter the primary
means of commuting between the islands was established by the government which
began operating barge and ferry service transportation In August 1997 a temporary
floating bridge was completed and opened for public use The floating bridge is
anticipated to remain in use until a new permanent bridge can be designed and
constructed
W O 3595 00 B Page 11
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION III SITE CHARACTERIZATION
A Geography
The Palau Islands form a curved chain of islands totaling about 350 in number
and covering approximately 458 square kilometers in area The island chain extends
approximately 161 kilometers in length and 64 kilometers in width Babeldaob the
largest island of the chain is an elongated volcanic island trending north to south and
encompasses about 208 square kilometers of land area Elevations on Babeldaob
range from sea level along the coastal areas to about 242 meters Mean Sea Level
MSL at Mt Ngerekelehuus on the northwestern side of Babeldaob
The Palau Reef encircles the island of Babeldaob as a barrier and fringing reef
creating extensive quiet water lagoons and bays with some deep channels and
passages adjacent to the island Beyond the fringing reef the ocean floor drops
steeply to greater than 300 meters in depth within a distance of about 1 kilometer
The island of Babeldaob is primarily of volcanic origin with some localized
occurrence of limestone rock formation particularly in southern coastal Babeldaob
The relief is generally characterized by hilly terrain of elongated ridgelines frequently
incised by streams and gullies exposing extremely weathered volcanic earth materials
Flatter alluvial areas are restricted mainly to the mouths and banks of larger streams
and along the coastline situated behind sandy beaches where inland hills do not
abruptly terminate at the shoreline More rugged terrain consisting of sharp ridges and
cliff lines occur on the western and southeastern portions of the island Both rounded
hilltops and sharp ridgelines rise above the generally rolling terrain at scattered
locations offering prominent geographic landmarks among the generally homogenous
backdrop
The coastline of Babeldaob is irregularly shaped with many small bays and
elevated headlands Swamp areas consisting of dense mangrove within shallow
tidal influenced mudflats exist throughout approximately 70 percent of the coastline
areas The width of the mangrove swamps along the coastline varies from less than
W O 3595 00 B Page 12
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION III SITE CHARACTERIZATION
10 meters to greater than 800 meters in some places The mangrove swamps
encompass much of the lowland coastline and large areas bordering the bays and
estuaries Marsh areas exist in some inland areas generally bordering major river
systems and broad basins
The drainage pattern on Babeldaob is essentially trellised with the larger streams
and rivers aligned with the longitudinal axis of the island Ngermeskang River is the
longest river measuring about 15 8 kilometers in length which flows into Karamando
Bay from the northeast The Ngerdok River is the largest watershed on Babeldaob
encompassing some 29 square kilometers in area
B Climate
The Palau Islands have a maritime tropical rainy climate characterized by small
seasonal changes Temperatures are generally uniform throughout the year with
abundant rainfall reaching a maximum in July and a minimum from February through
April The mean annual temperature is about 27 degrees Celsius with a relative
humidity of about 82 percent
Rainfall typically occurs as intense showers of relatively short duration and
averages about 250 to 500 mm per month Periods of prolonged heavy rainfall lasting
several days at a time occur as typhoon storm centers frequently pass to the north of
Palau during the summer months Other pronounced rainy periods occur as the
equatorial convergent zone advances northward within the vicinity of Palau around
June and July and again in September and October as the convergent zone retreats
southward
C Regional Geologic Setting
The Philippine Sea and the Pacific Ocean Basin are separated by a series of
elongated submarine ridge structures The Palau Islands are situated at the exposed
crest of the southwestern most submarine ridge of the area The Palau ridge is part of
W O 3595 00 B Page 13
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION Ill SITE CHARACTERIZATION
the Palau Kyushu Ridge which extends from Kyushu Japan southward towards Palau
where a complementary trench structure forms to the southeast of Palau These ridge
and trench structures constitute the Palau Arc The eastern slope of the Palau Ridge
slopes steeply to the Palau trench which plunges to about 8 200 meters at about
48 kilometers east of the north end of the Palau Islands The west flank of the ridge
slopes gradually to a depth of about 5 500 meters at about 400 kilometers to the west
The andesite line which marks the margin of the western Pacific Basin has
been positioned along the eastern edge of the Palau trench This demarcation
separates the region of predominantly andesitic volcanism to the west from the
Pacific Basin region of basaltic volcanism The area is also a major structural and
physiographic boundary between the two regions
The structure of the Palau Islands reflects their situation as the exposed crest of
the Palau Ridge The islands elongated form has resulted from volcanic emissions and
deposition of pyroclastic materials along the arcuate ridge structure Due to the varied
locations of the volcanic sources and the amount of emissions the successive
accumulation of pyroclastic materials was highly irregular in occurrence In addition
most of the eruptions were subaqueous resulting in submarine landslides and slumps
and contributing to the deformed and highly irregular character of the depositional
surfaces
D Geology of Babeldaob
Babeldaob Island exists as a result of the accumulation of volcanic materials
along the crest of the Palau Ridge The form of the island is principally controlled by
many factors which include 1 faulting associated with past tectonic activity
2 numerous historic land submergence and emergence as a result of sea level
fluctuation 3 submarine erosion 4 erosion by streams and 5 deep tropical
weathering of volcanic materials comprising the island
W O 3595 00 B Page 14
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION III SITE CHARACTERIZATION
In general Babeldaob consists of a central strip of the oldest volcanic rock
overlapped on the east by the next younger unit and separated by a fault zone on the
west from the youngest volcanic rocks which are arranged in a rough circle around a
former caldera at Karamando Bay The regional ridge and trench structure extensive
volcanism and the presence of numerous faults cutting the pyroclastic deposits confirm
past tectonic activity However at the present time there is little evidence of on going
deformation of the island arc system
Based on the Geology Map of Babelthuap and Adjacent Islands Palau Islands
prepared by the U S Army and the U S Geological Survey the geologic materials
mapped on Babeldaob include various volcanic alluvial and estuarine lagoonal or
beach deposits The most recent earth material deposits include man made fills
mangrove swamp mud alluvial sediments and coralline beach deposits These
materials continue to be deposited at the present time Terrestrial and marine
sediments deposited in historic Miocene through Pleistocene time include the alluvial
Airai clay with interbedded lignite and the Palau limestone formation The volcanic
materials comprise the oldest deposits and consist of the Babeldaob Aimeliik and
Ngeremlengui Formations These volcanic units comprise the bulk of the land area on
Babeldaob Island
The Babeldaob Formation consists of massive basaltic andesitic volcanic breccia
with some tuff breccia and layers of tuff U S Army 1956 Breccia is a coarse grained
volcanic rock composed of angular broken rock fragments or clasts welded together in
a finer grained mineral rock matrix Breccia is formed by volcanic explosions and or
debris flows of super heated rock mass Rocks and soils associated with this formation
exist as a large rectangular shaped area extending north northeast to south southwest
in central Babeldaob
The Aimeliik Formation consists of andesitic basaltic volcanic breccias tuff
breccia and bedded tuffs and is divided into the Ngarsul and Ngardok members which
W O 3595 00 B Page 15
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION III SITE CHARACTERIZATION
are composed of varying amounts of tuff and breccia materials U S Army 1956
The formation underlies most of northeastern eastern and southern Babeldaob
The Ngeremlengui Formation consists of andesitic and dacitic volcanic breccia
together with tuffs flows conglomerates and related sediments It is divided into three
members the Nghemesed dacitic volcanic breccia the
volcanic breccia and the Arakabesan andesitic volcanic breccia U S Army 1956
The formation occurs as a broad strip of area along the west central and northwest side
of Babeldaob and along the northern tip of Arekalong Peninsula
Other volcanic rock types include intrusive geologic bodies such as dikes sills
and volcanic plugs which occur widely distributed in the volcanic units described
above The larger intrusive rock structures can be found in the area around
Karamando Bay associated with the most recent volcanic center of that area
U S Army 1956 Many of these intrusive features are less weathered than their
surrounding host rock material and are erosional remnants exhibited as prominent
outcroppings
Because of the humid tropical climate the volcanic rock exposed at the surface
is usually extremely weathered to substantial depths with fresh surface outcroppings of
rock being generally rare in occurrence The majority of the volcanic materials
observed on Babeldaob Island have been weathered to residual and saprolite soils with
only scattered localized pockets of hard indurated rock The deep tropical weathering
of the island has resulted in a mature stage topography with rounded rolling hills
separated by scoured stream channels
The volcanic rocks of Babeldaob have been extensively faulted during and
following their deposition Faulting is believed to have been a major factor in
determining the distribution of volcanic formations as many geologic contacts occur
along fault lines U S Army 1956 Post volcanic faulting has modified the distribution
W O 3595 00 B Page 16
SECTION III SITE CHARACTERIZATION
of the geologic formations and is responsible for many physiographic features
Movement along the faults appeared to be similar to earlier tectonic movement
however the most recent movement is believed to be in response to new tectonic
forces which have since developed U S Army 1956 Based on the geologic map of
Babeldaob the larger fault zones curve to the northeast across the island forming
concave arcs
END OF SITE CHARACTERIZATION

SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
In general the proposed Palau Compact Road Package B alignment was
observed to traverse terrain underlain by six main soil and rock materials of varying
character and engineering properties The soil and rock materials were identified
during our geotechnical ground surface reconnaissance of the alignment and during our
subsurface exploration at selected locations along the alignment
The geotechnical reconnaissance included visual observation of both naturally
occurring exposures of the ground surface and exposures created by the bulldozer
during the trail clearing operations related to the drilling exploration In addition manual
probing of the surficial soils were performed at selected locations along the alignment to
evaluate the consistency of the near surface soils As a result of our site
reconnaissance and subsurface exploration the soil and rock materials observed were
condensed and grouped into six major soil or rock types The six main soil or rock
types are listed below in the general order of the frequency of occurrence throughout
the project site The listing begins with the most common materials encountered at the
site and ends with the least common type of material encountered
Saprolite Soil extremely weathered rock materials
Swamp Recent Alluvial Deposits organic mud and sediments
Undocumented Fill soil or rocky fills of unknown character
Lagoonal Deposits coralline sands and gravels
Older Alluvium consolidated silts and clays
Volcanic Breccia or Tuff Rock Formation relatively unweathered rock
materials
The following sections briefly describe the character of each of the above
generalized soil and rock types and how they relate to the soil and rock types outlined
in our Preliminary Geotechnical Engineering Report PGER dated
The relation is provided to serve as a link between the soil and rock descriptions
provided in our preliminary report and the condensed groups and descriptions of soil
and rock described in this report
W O 3595 00 B Page 18
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
A Saprolite Soil Extremely Weathered Rock
Saprolite is typical of the tropical weathering of volcanic rocks and is composed
mainly of silty materials The saprolite soil unit is the most dominant soil type traversed
by the entire length of the Package B Route This soil unit consists predominantly of
reddish brown mottled with tan purple and gray clayey silt and silty clay soils
The saprolite soils may contain variations in color tan grayish white or pinkish tan
with varying degrees of mottling or colored striations depending on the type of parent
volcanic rock from which the soils are derived and the degree of chemical weathering
that the material has experienced The soils are essentially derived from basaltic and
andesitic breccia and tuff formations which may contain intrusive rock bodies of
variable composition
Thin bauxite gravel deposits consisting of a loose surface cover of brown and
red bauxite concretions are found in scattered locations mantling the residual and
saprolite soils Based on our observations the bauxite gravels are generally confined
to the drier upper slopes and ridgelines of sparse vegetation The deposits are
generally absent on lower hill slopes and areas covered by dense forest vegetation
The absence of bauxite gravel in these areas may be attributed to higher soil moisture
content and accelerated chemical weathering processes The bauxite gravel is
generally high in iron and aluminum content The thickness of the bauxite deposits vary
but are generally less than about 200 mm thick
The occurrence of buried relatively unweathered hard rock such as massive
boulders or zones of less weathered rocky material localized intrusive volcanic bodies
such as dikes and sills and irregular transitions to underlying rock formation may be
embedded within the saprolite soil type The occurrence of these rock zones within the
saprolite are common but they may be difficult to locate by surface observation and
may not be encountered by test borings
W O 3595 00 B Page 19
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
The saprolite soil unit described herein may be equated to Soil Types C D E
and F described in our PGER The Soil Types outlined in our preliminary report have
been revised and grouped together to simplify the classification of the saprolite and
residual soil geologic materials The reduction in the number of soil types is due to
similarities in the physical characteristics and engineering properties of the various
residual and saprolite soils encountered at the site
B Swamp and Recent Alluvial Deposits
Based on their characteristics and modes of deposition the swamp soils and
recent alluvial soils are closely related to each other in physical properties Both of
these soil deposits generally exist as under consolidated soft to medium stiff deposits
as a result of their sedimentary deposition These deposits underlie relatively localized
portions of the proposed alignment and are generally found at the lower elevations
bordering the swamp land and associated with the occurrence of the larger streams or
rivers
The swamp soils generally consist of dark brown or dark gray organic rich silts
and clayey silts with some sand and gravel These soils may contain significant
amounts of root and decomposed organic material peat as a result of organic debris
being buried during deposition The marsh and swamp deposits are commonly found
along the low lying coastal mangrove areas where streams meet the shoreline
environment and where shallow groundwater levels are largely influenced by tidal
fluctuation and stream discharge The ground surface within the swamp land may be
very soft existing as a slurry of mud and water or may be relatively firm as a result of
the intertwined matrix of root growth associated with mangrove vegetation
The recent alluvial deposits generally consist of tan to brown clayey silts and silty
clays derived from the erosion transportation and re deposition of saprolite and
residual soil materials Alluvial soils are generally found within some stream channels
and bordering some stream banks at the mouths outlets of streams and within broad
W O 3595 00 B Page 20
GEOLABS HAWAI
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
valley floors and basin features surrounded by hills These soils may also be found in
close proximity to swamp and tidal flat environments Furthermore recent alluvium
may be found interbedded with the swamp and tidal flat soil deposits
The swamp and recent alluvial soil unit described herein may be equated to
Soil Types H and described in our PGER Soil Types H and outlined in our
preliminary report have been condensed and regrouped to simplify the classification of
the materials encountered
C Undocumented Fill
The undocumented fill observed at the site essentially consist of two distinct
types The first type may be described generally as soil material mixed with some rock
fragments consisting of clay and silt with some sand gravel and cobble materials
These fill materials were derived from the reworking excavating and leveling of the
existing road base and periodic importation of sandy gravel coral and rock cobbles as
efforts to improve traction on the existing road surface The fills were placed for the
maintenance of the existing Babeldaob Road that intersects portions of the proposed
Palau Compact Road alignment
The construction and maintenance of the Babeldaob Road was observed to
affect the Palau Compact Road alignment in that some of the fills may have been
deposited within the proposed alignment as potentially loose or soft fill slopes bordering
the existing road During our exploration the soils were observed to be spread
periodically by a bulldozer to provide for improved road surface conditions Compaction
of the soils on the road surface was achieved with the heavy equipment and passing
traffic In contrast the fill slopes were generally observed as loose overcast material
The second type of fill observed at the site is related to the earth materials used
for the construction of the existing Ngiwal Causeway The materials generally include
dredged coralline detritus and sediments consisting of coral and shell fragments with
W O 3595 00 B Page 21
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
sand and silt Field observations indicate the finer fill materials may have been placed
over a base bedding consisting of coral cobbles and boulders mixed with gravels
sands and silts The finer materials appear to comprise the upper surface of the fills
The construction practice and quality control of the causeway fills are unknown
D Lagoonal Deposits
The lagoonal deposits at the site generally consist of gray white or tan silty
coralline sands and gravels with shells derived from coral reef and beach environments
Included within these deposits may be lenses of gray or brown clayey silts with gravel
or dark gray peat The lagoonal deposits are typically under consolidated and
accumulate as loose or soft deposits in submarine low energy environments such as
the tidal influenced bays estuaries and lagoons located in the vicinity of the Ngiwal
Causeway The deposits accumulate as a result of the transportation and deposition of
broken coral reef materials and periodic influx of terrestrial sediment and organic matter
introduced from streams flowing into the shallow water depositional environment
The lagoonal deposit soil unit described herein may be equated to Soil Type J
described in our PGER
E Older Alluvium
Old alluvium deposits are generally stiff silty and clayey soils that were originally
deposited in alluvial environments buried over long periods of time by more recent
deposits to become somewhat consolidated and then subsequently uncovered at the
ground surface by erosion or other geologic processes The deposits may resemble
saprolite soil or may show signs of bedding and include layers of varied silts and clays
with some embedded seams of organic materials such as peat or lignite These soils
were generally encountered as localized occurrences in the Airai portion of the
proposed alignment and in the vicinity of major stream crossings
Old alluvium may be identified as light tan brown or reddish colored
sedimentary silt and clay deposits The deposits may contain thin layers of black clayey
W O 3595 00 B Page 22
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
silt representing organic rich lignite which may be identified by a characteristic organic
odor The deposits may resemble saprolite soil deposits but are clearly differentiable by
the layered characteristic For this report the deposits have been grouped separately
from saprolite because of the presence of embedded layers of varying soil character
The layering may have the potential to develop slippage or fracture surfaces at the
layer interfaces when exposed in a cut slope condition as an inclined bed sloping into a
cut slope face The old alluvium soil unit described herein may be equated to
Soil Type G described in our PGER
F Volcanic Breccia or Tuff Rock Formation Relatively Unweathered Rock
The volcanic breccia and tuff rock units occur as greenish to brownish gray
slightly fractured to massive hard rock formation The rock formations typically exist as
massive rounded outcroppings showing embedded breccia clasts or as layered
fractured often platy volcanic tuff Ground surface exposures of the rock formations
are generally rare and occur intermittently throughout the alignment
Volcanic breccia are angular pyroclastic rock materials erupted from vents as
either flows of superheated material or as blocks of superheated material larger than
60 mm in size that may be cemented with or without a volcanic material matrix
Volcanic tuff is formed by the deposition and cementation of relatively fine grained
pyroclastic materials such as sand and ash which accumulate as airfall deposits
during volcanic eruptions of superheated materials and gases Tuff formations often
show horizontal or inclined bedding which mimic the underlying topography that the
deposit accumulated These rock formations may be exposed at the ground surface
partially exposed and coexisting with some saprolite soil or buried under a relatively
thin mantle of surficial alluvium or residual soil
The rock formation unit described herein may be equated to Soil Rock Types A
and B described in our PGER The rock types outlined in our preliminary report have
been revised and condensed to simplify the classification of the rock formation
W O 3595 00 B Page 23
GFOI I ARS HAWAH
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
materials The reduction of rock types is due to similarities in the physical
characteristics and engineering properties of the various rock materials encountered at
the site

In general the terrain underlain by the saprolite soils consists of an irregular

accumulations overlying saprolite soil within some drainage channels Most of

steep stream gradients the channelized flow character and the flash flood
run off experienced
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
In general the topographic lows including valleys gullies and basins show
much wetter surface soil conditions than the adjacent hills or ridgelines
indicating potential slow seepage or wicking of subsurface moisture and poor
drying due to the forest canopy In contrast the ground surface of the upper
slopes and ridgelines appeared to dry out between rainstorms
3 Undocumented Fills
Approximately one half of the Package B portion of the East Route contains
significant stretches of alignment that follows the existing Babeldaob Road
Because of the need for on going maintenance of the existing dirt road it has
been observed that multiple generations of variable fill material have been
placed to raise the road grade and to provide for improved traction during rainy
seasons Methods of road maintenance observed at the site include the
following 1 road widening by clearing of the shoulder vegetation 2 reworking
and compaction of the existing road base and 3 importation and spreading of
various materials including clay and granular materials such as coral gravel and
rock cobbles
The fills associated with the road maintenance are believed to be generally thin
however the fill materials may be described as anomalous to the native soil
types encountered and mapped along the alignment The previous table that
summarizes the geologic and soil conditions encountered along the alignment
does not account for the occurrence of surficial fill materials including any
reworked soil coral rubble or cobbles and boulders that may have been utilized
for road fill Therefore it should be noted that variable materials related to the
pre existing fills could be encountered periodically within the Palau Compact
Road alignment during construction
A primary concern regarding the pre existing fills is the potential existence of
loose or soft overcast and under compacted fill materials that may encroach
within the Package B portion of the Palau Compact Road alignment Therefore

5 Typical Soil Profile for Saprolite Soil Condition
Based on our reconnaissance observations it is possible to define a typical soil
profile for areas mapped as saprolite soils The profile appears to vary
somewhat between saprolite soil condition existing in forested areas and the
saprolite soil condition observed in savanna areas Due to the thick forest
canopy and growth of a variety of trees shrubs and ground cover the soil
profile in forested areas may be include the following

SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
This is a typical profile as may be observed in the field however not all forested
locations may exhibit these layers In addition thicknesses may vary
considerably or certain layers may be absent from the profile The intent of the
typical soil profile is to provide a general indication of the amount of potential
deleterious organic materials to be removed during grubbing operations
In comparison to forest environments the savanna environment is typically
devoid of significant forest litter and the topsoil horizon is usually very thin or
absent due to a lack of supply of organic material and generally higher rates of
erosion As previously indicated bauxite gravel deposits are common on the
hilltop savanna environments and seem to replace the occurrence of forest litter
and organic topsoil horizons In general the more extensive savanna conditions
were observed in the northern half of the alignment from the existing road
intersection leading to Ngchesar and continuing along the proposed alignment to
the existing road intersection leading to Ngiwal
6 Typical Soil Profile for Swamp Recent Alluvial Deposits
The areas mapped and defined as swamp and recent alluvial deposits
throughout the alignment are typically found at low lying saturated or very moist
ground conditions These deposits generally consist of under consolidated soft
to very soft organic silts and clays containing a high content of decomposed
organic materials These areas may exist as coastal tidal flats that are
influenced by tidal fluctuations or may border streams or localized swamp areas
of groundwater seepage The vegetation encountered ranges from dense
mangrove to tall grass or may contain dense groves of palm trees
The mangrove areas often exhibit a ground surface consisting of an intertwined
matrix of root growth at and extending below the ground surface that serves as a
bridge over the very soft and saturated ground conditions
W O 3595 00 B Page 33
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
T Typical Inland Stream Channel Characteristics
Many of the stream channels observed crossing the alignment exhibit similar
characteristics In general two types of drainage morphologies were observed
The first type is typical of active perennial stream flow of moderate to high
discharge volume These streams are more commonly acting as primary mid to
lower reach well developed channels discharging larger size watersheds
The second drainage morphology appears as a result of generally lighter stream
flow or spring seepage and is contained within broad U shaped gullies The
gully contains a broader area of slower moving stream flow or seepage
Most of the perennial streams are situated within U shaped gullies incising
saprolite soil The active stream channel was often observed further incised at
the gully invert as a steep sided meandering trench exposing the geologic
character of the gully bottom The larger stream channel inverts were often
scoured and exposed highly weathered and or slightly weathered hard rock
formation Alluvial deposits associated with perennial stream channel
morphology appear relatively insignificant
Most of the intermittent slower flowing streams exist within broad U shaped gully
bottoms covered by a dense matrix of intertwined roots and some surficial soft
alluvial deposits Commonly this drainage morphology was observed in the
upper weakly developed reaches of streams and locations where several gullies
converge to form a single broad drainage gully Alluvial soil accumulations and
the occurrence of a matrix of exposed root growth are more prevalent associated
with this stream morphology
H Subsurface Conditions
The subsurface conditions along the Package B alignment were explored by
drilling and sampling a total of 38 borings at the approximate locations shown on the
Site Plans Plates 3 1 through 3 3 In general the majority of the Package B alignment
W O 3595 00 B Page 34
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
traverses saprolite soils derived from intense weathering of the volcanic breccia and tuff
rock formation Based on the borings drilled in this area pockets of variably weathered
rock may be embedded within the saprolite soil These pockets may contain saprolite
material of a sandy or gravelly nature in contrast to the typical clayey silt and silty clay
saprolite soil composition In addition relatively unweathered parent rock material
or other volcanic intrusive rock may be locally embedded in the saprolite soil matrix
These rock bodies may exist as erosional remnant material The erosional remnants
may occur as boulders ranging in size from 1 meter to in excess of about 6 meters
Based on the boring information hard rock formation consisting of volcanic
breccia and some tuff formation should be expected to be at variable depths below the
saprolite soils The depth to rock can be highly variable depending on the local
weathering and erosion rates In general rock formation underlying some prominent
hills were encountered at depths ranging from about 5 to 20 meters below the ground
surface Rock formation was also encountered at shallower depths on the order of
about 2 to 4 meters below the ground surface but these locations were generally
restricted to topographic low locations bordering streams or deeply incised gullies
Based on our boring information and reconnaissance data excavations
proposed at some of the existing steeper and more prominent hill slopes will likely
expose rock formation at relatively shallower depths than excavations made in less
prominent hill slopes In addition boulder remnants embedded in a saprolite matrix
may be encountered more frequently in the prominent steeper hill slopes or ridgelines
Our exploration at the lagoon and estuary environments situated at the northern
segment of the East Route indicates that very loose and soft silty coralline sands and
gravels consisting of lagoonal and beach sediments may extend to significant depths
below the existing lagoon ground level Based on the boring data the thickness of the
loose soft lagoonal deposits located near the proposed bridge locations may be on the
order of about 18 to 20 meters below the lagoon mudline However the sediments
W O 3595 00 B Page 35
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
appear to overlie the buried weathered rock formation as indicated by the stiff saprolite
soils encountered
Groundwater levels were encountered in some of the drilled borings at variable
depths below the existing ground surface at the time of our field exploration Generally
groundwater was encountered in borings drilled near active streams and in low elevations
near the coastline Groundwater levels can fluctuate depending on factors such as tidal
fluctuations seasonal rainfall presence of springs and or seepage storm surge
conditions time of year and other factors
Because of the high tropical rainfall coupled with low permeability soils surface
run off is generally high However because of the infiltration that does occur seepage of
the downward percolating groundwater may be observed along the lower slopes of hills
and ridgelines The seepage areas are reflected by changes in the growth of vegetation
and the occurrence of perpetually moist ground surface conditions The seepage is
widespread and occasionally may produce a flowing spring where a layer of more
permeable soil or rock transmits the flow of water to the ground surface Other seepage
may occur at the interface where saprolite soil is in abrupt contact with underlying
massive rock formation
Detailed descriptions of the field exploration methodology are presented in
Appendix A of this report Descriptions and graphic representations of the materials
encountered in the drilled borings are provided on the Logs of Borings Plates A 1 1
through A 38 1 Laboratory tests were performed on selected samples and the results
are presented in Appendix B

SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
Based on our literature research site reconnaissance and field exploration
performed for Package B of the Palau Compact Road project we anticipate that the
proposed roadway alignment will traverse various volcanic sedimentary alluvial
mangrove swamp and lagoonal deposits as well as undocumented fills The observed
soil rock materials ranged from very dense volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock formation to
medium stiff to very stiff saprolite soils and to very soft and or loose recent alluvial
mangrove swamp and coralline lagoonal deposits
The earthwork for this project constitutes a major portion of the construction costs
Therefore the design slopes for cuts and fills have a significant impact on the construction
budget Flatter conservative slope ratios generally increase slope stability However in
the mountainous terrain along the proposed roadway alignment flatter slope ratios result
in greatly increased earthwork quantities and erosion potential Therefore for this project
somewhat steeper slope ratios have been adopted We believe that the reduced
earthwork quantities and reduced erosion potential outweigh the potential for localized
sloughing of some of the steeper cut and fill slopes However a more vigorous slope
repair and roadway maintenance effort should be expected for the roadway
Based on the subsurface conditions anticipated along the proposed alignment we
believe that slope inclinations of 1H 1V and 2H 1V may be used for the design of the
planned cut and fill slopes respectively We believe that a cut slope inclination steeper
than 1H 1V may be feasible in areas where very dense volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock
formations are encountered Depending on the heights of the planned fill slopes fill slopes
may be designed with a slope inclination as steep as 1H 1V except in soft soil areas
provided that adequate soil reinforcements are incorporated into the fill material
Geolabs Hawaii should be consulted to provide site specific recommendations pertaining
to cut and fill slopes with a slope inclination steeper than the general values recommended
above
W O 3595 00 B Page 37
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
We wish to emphasize that drainage features such as interceptor drainage ditches
subdrains road gutters and longitudinal edge drains are critical to the stability of the cut
and fill slopes and performance of the pavement structure Excessive surface run off over
the slope face may cause erosion of the exposed soils thus potentially jeopardizing the
long term stability and performance of the cut and fill slopes Accumulation of water below
the pavement structural section will soften the silty and clayey subgrade soils and cause
premature failure of the pavement structure Therefore it is our opinion that special
attention should be given to the design and implementation of these drainage features
along the proposed roadway alignment
The roadway alignment near Ngerdoch Lake from about to
of Package B was re aligned for about 0 9 kilometers to avoid archaeological
sites in this area Additional field exploration was conducted at selected locations along
the proposed Package B re alignment to provide the necessary information for the
formulation of the geotechnical engineering recommendations presented herein
Construction of a causeway embankment Ngiwal Causeway between about
and is anticipated for Package B The causeway embankment
will be constructed over soft loose lagoonal deposits and adjacent to the existing
causeway embankment Therefore placement of the causeway fills should be initiated as
early as possible to allow the existing ground to adjust to the new fill loads A settlement
waiting period will need to be specified in the contract documents and a settlement
monitoring program should be implemented to evaluate the magnitude and rate of the
estimated settlements prior to construction of the pavement section and improvements
such as the causeway bridge foundations abutments and culverts on the causeway fills
A surcharge program may be considered to accelerate the consolidation of the underlying
soft loose soils to reduce the settlement waiting period
For the purpose of our discussions fill height is defined as the vertical distance
between the top and toe elevations of the fill slope whereas fill thickness is defined as the
vertical distance between the existing ground and the finished grade at any point Detailed
discussion of these items and our geotechnical engineering design recommendations for
W O 3595 00 B Page 38
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
earthwork related items are presented in the following sections of this report Discussion
and recommendations for the design of structures such as bridge foundations abutment
walls and box culverts etc are presented in Section VI of this report
A Earthwork
Based on the plans provided and the rolling topography at the project site
earthwork for the proposed Package B roadway construction will involve excavations on
the order of about 24 meters deep and embankments up to about 15 meters thick
The majority of the embankment fill materials will be generated from the planned
excavations along the proposed alignment Based on the geologic conditions along the
proposed alignment we anticipate that the excavated materials would range from
medium stiff to very stiff saprolite soils to very dense volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock
In addition the earthwork construction will also encounter some soft and or loose recent
alluvial mangrove swamp and coralline lagoonal deposits
Items of earthwork that are addressed in the subsequent subsections include the
following 1 Cut Slope Design 2 Fill Slope Design Site
Preparation 5 Fills and Backfills 6 Fill Placement and Compaction Requirements
7 Excavation 8 Boulder Disposal and 9 Earthwork Quantities
1 Cut Slope Design
Based on the subsurface conditions anticipated along the proposed alignment we
believe that the planned cut slopes may expose materials ranging from medium stiff
to very stiff saprolite materials to very dense and or hard volcanic breccia and tuff
rock formation In general we believe that a cut slope inclination of 1H 1V or flatter
may be used for the design of the planned cut slopes along the proposed
alignment In addition it is our opinion that a cut slope inclination as steep as
may be used in localized areas where very dense volcanic breccia and
hard tuff rock formation are encountered However we did not encounter dense
rock formation at shallow depths over an extensive portion of the roadway
alignment where steepening the cut slope for the rock formation can be effectively
implemented
W O 3595 00 B Page 39
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
Where the steeper cut slope inclination is used for cut slope design in rock
formation a rockfall catchment ditch should be provided at the toe of the steep rock
cut slope General guidelines for the design of the rockfall catchment ditch are
provided on Plate 4 of this report We recommend that Geolabs Hawaii be
consulted for any other planned cut slope where a cut slope inclination steeper than
1H 1V is desired
As previously indicated we anticipate that the proposed roadway alignment may
traverse areas with pre existing buried faults and joints which may result in
potential block type failure of the planned cut slopes Therefore it is our opinion
that planned cut slopes at these areas may need to be modified with a flatter slope
inclination that matches the angle of these potential slip planes These areas will
not be evident until exposed by the excavation process during construction
Therefore the cut slopes should be mapped by an engineer geologist from our
office or a qualified engineer geologist during construction to further evaluate the
cut slopes
Excessive surface run off over the slope face may cause erosion of the exposed
soils thus potentially jeopardizing the long term stability and performance of the cut
slope Therefore cut slopes should be protected by appropriate slope planting or
by other means such as placement of geotextile fabrics on the slope face
immediately after the slope is excavated to reduce the potential for erosion of the
exposed soils Detailed discussions pertaining to the use of geotextile fabrics on
the slope face are presented in the Erosion Control section of this report
For cut slopes with vertical heights greater than 15 meters we recommend that a
minimum 2 4 meter wide bench be provided at the mid point of the slope to reduce
the potential for erosion due to surface run off water The slope benches may be
omitted for cut slopes in the very dense volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock
formation encountered in localized areas Where slope benches are provided
drainage ditches should be provided on the benches to collect and divert surface
water on the slopes to appropriate discharge outlets The drainage ditches and
W O 3595 00 B Page 40
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
discharge outlets should be lined with 50 mm thick fiber reinforced shotcrete or
gunite or 100 mm concrete to reduce erosion from the concentrated flows
In addition interceptor drainage ditches should be considered at the top of the cut
slopes to provide proper drainage of surface run off water Interceptor drainage
ditches with steep grades may be susceptible to erosion and may require lining with
50 mm thick fiber reinforced shotcrete or gunite In lieu of the shotcrete or gunite
lining consideration may be given to the use of 100 mm thick concrete or other
channel lining material such as turf reinforcement mats
Due to budgetary constraints we understand that the slope benches recommended
in our preliminary geotechnical engineering report and above will likely be
eliminated entirely for the Palau Compact Road project We believe that elimination
of slope benches along certain segments of the roadway alignments may result in
potential for instability of the planned cut slopes such as sloughing and or localized
slope failures Therefore the Owner should be made aware that this will probably
result in a more vigorous slope repair and roadway maintenance program in the
future
It should be noted that the planned cut slopes of 1H 1V slope ratio are steep
Therefore in the event that slight over cutting of a slope occurs or the cut slope is
slightly damaged by erosion consideration should be given to leaving the slope as
is rather than attempting to backfill the slope to the design grade with sliver fills If
backfilling of an over cut slope is necessary over steepened or unstable the cut
slope should be completely over cut and buttressed with compacted fill 3 meters
wide constructed of cement treated subbase by keying and benching the fill
materials into the over cut slope
2 Fill Slope Design
As previously mentioned the on site saprolite soils have high in situ moisture
contents Considering the high moisture contents of the on site soils the
compaction criteria have been reduced from the normal 90 percent to a minimum of
W O 3595 00 B Page 41
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
85 percent relative compaction in order to aid the earthwork construction in this
high rainfall environment using high moisture tropical soils In general permanent
embankment fills constructed with the lower compaction criteria over firm to stiff
ground should be designed with a slope inclination no steeper than 2H 1V to allow
for the reduced fill strength
If necessary we believe that a steeper fill slope inclination of may be
used for fill heights up to about 4 meters except in areas where soft subsoils are
anticipated This would not require selective grading of the more favorable
materials which generally exist only in thin horizons to be placed in designated
areas of the steeper fill slopes Where the fill height exceeds about 4 meters soil
reinforcements using reinforced slope geogrids or geotextiles should be
incorporated into the design of the steepened fill slope
It should be noted that the steeper fill slope ratio or steeper should not
be used for embankments constructed of general fill constructed over the soft
and or loose alluvial and mangrove swamp deposits to reduce the potential for fill
slope failures Our field reconnaissance suggests that soft and wet soils are
present along the roadway alignments Potential areas where soft subsoils may be
encountered are presented in the Soft Ground Stabilization section of this report
If the conditions warrant a steeper fill slope inclination fill slopes may be designed
with a slope inclination as steep as 1H 1V except in areas where soft subsoils are
anticipated provided that the fill slopes are reinforced with geogrids or similar
materials as discussed in the Reinforced Earth Slopes section of this report
We recommend that Geolabs Hawaii be consulted for _ site specific
recommendations for any planned fill slopes with a slope inclination steeper than
2H 1V along the proposed roadway alignment
We understand that steepened slopes are planned between
and 25 668 of the Package B East Route alignment The maximum
fill height in this section of the steepened fill slope is about 5 meters Although the
W O 3595 00 B Page 42
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
steepened fill slope is higher than 4 meters we believe that reinforced slope
geogrids or geotextiles will not be required since the fill is constructed on top of a
concrete box culvert and the segment is relatively short
Fills to be placed on existing slopes with an inclination steeper than 5H 1V should
be benched into the existing slope to provide stability of the new fill embankment
against sliding as shown on Plate 5 The filling operations should start at the
lowest point and continue up in level horizontal compacted layers in accordance
with the fill placement recommendations presented in the Fill Placement and
Compaction Requirements subsection of this report Fill slopes should be
constructed by overfilling and cutting back to the design slope ratio to obtain a
well compacted slope face
For fill slopes with a vertical height greater than 6 meters we recommend that a
key be constructed at the toe of the fill slope to provide stability of the new fill
embankment against sliding The key should be embedded into stiff soils or at
least 0 5 meters below the lowest adjacent grade In addition the base width of the
key should be at least 3 meters A typical sketch of keying and benching is
provided on Plate 5
Excessive water should be diverted away from the tops of slopes and slope
planting should be provided as soon as the fill slopes are completed to reduce
potential erosion of the finished slopes In general slope benches are not required
for the planned fill slopes except at site specific locations Where slope benches
are necessary we recommend that a minimum 2 4 meter wide bench be provided
at the mid point of the slope to reduce the potential for erosion due to surface
run off water Construction of earth berms interceptor drainage ditches and the
use of geotextile fabrics over the fill slope face should be considered to reduce the
potential for erosion thus enhancing the long term stability of the planned fill
slopes
