have been presented in Section V Causeway Fill section of this report
SECTION VI DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS
G Structure Approach Slabs
As previously indicated placement of new fills at the abutments will induce
consolidation of the soft loose recent alluvial and lagoonal deposits underlying the
abutment locations Settlements on the order of about 500 to 1500 mm due to placement
of about 5 to 12 meters of fills have been estimated for these bridge abutments Post
construction settlements of the abutment fills are estimated to be between 50 and 75 mm
Asa result of these anticipated post construction settlements we recommend that
structure approach slabs be provided at the abutment locations to reduce the potential for
abrupt differential settlements between the drilled shaft and driven pile supported bridge
structure and the abutment fill placed over soft loose soils
The structure approach slab should be supported on a minimum of 200 mm of
subbase course placed on a prepared subgrade The subgrade should be scarified to a
depth of about 200 mm moisture conditioned to at least 2 percent above the optimum
moisture content and compacted to not less than 90 percent relative compaction The
subbase course should be moisture conditioned to above the optimum moisture content
and compacted to at least 95 percent relative compaction
H Retaining Structures
All retaining structures including abutment walls box culverts wing walls etc
should be designed to resist the lateral earth pressures due to the adjacent soils and
surcharge effects The recommended lateral earth pressures for design of retaining
structures expressed in equivalent fluid pressures are presented below Parameters for
design of foundations for these retaining structures are discussed in the Box Culverts and
Wing Walls section of this report

In general an active condition may be used for gravity walls or walls that are free to
deflect by as much as 0 5 percent of the wall height If the tops of the walls are not free to
W O 3595 00 B Page 108
SECTION VI DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS
deflect beyond this degree or are restrained the walls should be designed for the at rest
condition These lateral earth pressures do not include hydrostatic pressures therefore it
is imperative that a proper subdrainage system be incorporated in the construction details
Retaining walls should be well drained to reduce the build up of hydrostatic
pressures A typical drainage system would consist of a 300 mm wide zone of drain rock
immediately around a perforated pipe perforations down at the base of the wall
discharging to an appropriate outlet or weepholes As an alternative a prefabricated
drainage product such as MiraDrain or EnkaDrain may be used in lieu of the drainage
material The prefabricated drainage product should also be hydraulically connected to a
perforated pipe at the base of the wall which is daylighted for free drainage Backfill
behind the permeable drainage zone may consist of general fill or granular fill material
depending on the design parameters used Unless covered by concrete slabs or
pavements the upper 300 mm of backfill should consist of low expansion impervious
material general fill to reduce water infiltration behind the walls
Surcharge stresses due to areal surcharges line loads and point loads within a
horizontal distance equal to the depth of the wall should be considered in the design For
uniform surcharge stresses imposed on the loaded side of the wall a rectangular
distribution with uniform pressure equal to the following percentage active or at rest
conditions of the vertical surcharge pressure acting on the entire height of the wall may be
used in design Additional analyses during design may be needed to evaluate the
surcharge effects of point loads and line loads

Box Culverts and Wing Walls
We envision that reinforced concrete box culverts with wing walls will be required
for drainage purposes at some of the stream crossings and for the circulation culverts in
SECTION VI DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS
the causeway embankment for the proposed roadway project In addition wing walls for
the numerous pipe culverts will also be constructed for this project In general we
anticipate that shallow foundations bearing on the stiff saprolite soils encountered at the
project site or the recommended working platform or stabilization layer for soft ground
stabilization may be utilized for support of the planned reinforced concrete box culvert and
wing wall structures Based on the field exploration results we believe that the following
values may be used to evaluate the bearing support sliding resistance and passive
pressure resistance of the planned structures based on LRFD methods

A 200 mm gravel cushion layer should be provided between the bottom of the box
culvert and the underlying foundation soils to provide more uniform bearing support
The gravel cushion layer should consist of drain rock A schematic detail of the cushion
layer is provided on Plate 20 Where the box culverts will be subjected to heavy
overburden pressures due to high embankment fills we recommend that the thickness of
the gravel cushion layer be increased in accordance with the guidelines provided on
Plate 20
Based on a service limit state bearing pressure of 150 kPa we estimate that
foundation settlements under the anticipated design loads for foundations bearing on the
stiff saprolite soils to be less than 25 mm
In general foundations should be embedded a minimum of 500 mm below the
lowest adjacent finish grades If foundations are located next to utility trenches or
W O 3595 00 B e RES Page 110
SECTION VI DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS
easements they should be embedded below a 1H 1V imaginary plane extending upward
from the bottom edge of the utility trench or as deep as the inverts of the utility lines This
requirement is necessary to avoid surcharging adjacent below grade structures with
additional structural loads and to reduce the potential for foundation settlement
Lateral loads acting on the structure may be resisted by frictional resistance
between the base of the foundation and the bearing soil and by passive earth pressure
developed against the near vertical faces of the embedded portion of the foundation The
values presented in the table above may be used to evaluate the passive pressure
resistance for footings embedded and bearing on the stiff saprolite soils or stabilization
layer in soft soil areas A reduced value of 25 kN m extreme even limit state should be
used for foundations embedded below the groundwater level Unless covered by
pavements or slabs the passive resistance in the upper 300 mm should be neglected
J Pipe Culverts
Numerous pipe culverts are planned for this project In general a granular bedding
consisting of 150 mm of drain rock is recommended under pipe culverts If soft and or
loose soils are encountered at the proposed pipe inverts an additional 500 mm of drain
rock wrapped in a non woven geotextile such as Mirafi 180N or equivalent should be
provided below the bedding layer for more uniform support Drain rock should also be
used for the initial backfill up to the springline of the pipe 0 5 times the pipe diameter to
provide adequate support around the pipes For larger pipe culverts exceeding 600 mm in
diameter we believe that the initial backfill may be reduced to 0 25 times the outside pipe
diameter measured from the top of the bedding layer as shown on Plate 21
Where groundwater is present above the pipe drain rock should be used as backfill
up to at least 200 mm above the water level It is critical that free draining materials be
used for the initial backfill to reduce the potential for formation of voids below the haunches
of pipes and to provide adequate support for the sides of the pipes which could result in
settlement of the backfill and damage to the pipes The use of sand as backfill materials
SECTION VI DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS
around the pipe culverts should be prohibited due to the potential for migration or loss of
fines during heavy rains which may result in potential ground settlement and pavement
distress
The upper portion of the trench backfill from the level of the springline of the pipes
or above the initial backfill level as recommended for larger diameter pipes to the top of
the subgrade or finished grade may consist of general fill with a maximum particle size of
less than 150 mm The backfill material should be moisture conditioned to at least
2 percent above the optimum moisture placed in maximum 200 mm level loose lifts and
mechanically compacted to not less than 85 percent relative compaction If the pipe
culverts are backfilled in a trench after completion of the grading operations we
recommend that the upper 1 meter of the trench backfill below the pavement subgrade be
compacted to at least 90 percent relative compaction A typical section of the trench
details is presented on Plate 21
For the reinforced concrete pipe culverts a minimum cover of 0 75 meters should
be maintained above the top of the pipes to the finish grades in order to facilitate
construction of the pavement structure Where the longitudinal gradients of the reinforced
concrete pipe culverts are 20 percent or steeper the lower three pipe segments of the
concrete pipe should be supported on a concrete cradle near the outlet end of the culvert
to anchor the pipe culverts and to restrain the culverts from lateral movement due to
potential scour The outlet wall structure should also be properly keyed into stiff soils to
anchor the pipes A typical section of the concrete cradle is provided on Plate 22
The concrete cradle may also be used in areas where substantial fills are placed over the
culverts to increase the bedding factors
K Soft Soil Stabilization Under Pipe and Box Culverts
Soft and wet soils will be encountered at the foundation subgrade levels at some of
the drainage crossings Some of these potential areas have been presented in Section V
Soft Ground Stabilization section of this report In areas where the drainage structures
are underlain by relatively thin soft soil deposits on the order of 1 to 2 meters below the
bottom of the drainage structure elevation we recommend that these soft and wet soils
W O 3595 00 B F291 PONENT Page 112
SECTION VI DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS
be removed to expose the underlying firm soils prior to backfilling with suitable fills and
construction of the drainage structures We recommend that contract documents include
additive and deductive unit prices for over excavation to remove soft soils and suitable fill
placement as a contingency item to account for variations in the over excavation
quantities
For drainage structures underlain by significant soft soil deposits but with relatively
thin fills fills less than about 5 meters thick we believe that the fill embankment may be
constructed with a temporary drainage structure followed by a settlement waiting period to
allow the anticipated settlements to occur After the settlements have occurred and are
near equilibrium the temporary drainage structure may be excavated and removed
followed by construction of the permanent drainage structure For the box culverts we
recommend that a 1 2 meter thick layer of drain rock wrapped in a woven geotextile Mirafi
600X or equivalent with 1200 or equivalent be incorporated into the
stabilization layer to improve the bearing capacity of the soft soils as shown on Plate 20
Due to the large widths of the box culverts a relatively thick stabilization layer with soil
reinforcements is recommended to provide a firm foundation for the box culverts For the
pipe culverts a stabilization layer consisting of 500 mm of drain rock wrapped in a
non woven geotextile Mirafi 18ON or equivalent should be provided below the cushion
layer for more uniform support as shown on Plate 21 and discussed in the Pipe Culverts
section of this report
In areas where the drainage structures are underlain by significant soft soil deposits
and with substantial fills fills greater than 5 meters thick we believe that the permanent
drainage structures located in these soft soil areas will be subjected to a substantial
amount of settlements resulting from consolidation of the soft soil deposits under the
substantial fill loads In order to reduce the effects of the substantial settlements on the
drainage structures we recommend that the soft soil deposits underneath these drainage
structures be removed and replaced with suitable fill materials prior to their installation
The approximate lateral limits of the soft soil removal and suitable fill replacement is
shown on Plate 11 Schematic Detail Soft Soil Removal Under Drainage Structures
W O 3595 00 B GEOLARSHRWAI Page 113
SECTION VI DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS
After installation of the drainage structures stage construction may then proceed for these
soft soil areas with substantial fill loads as discussed in Section V Special Earthwork
Requirements section of this report
L Waterlines
We understand that new waterlines relocation of existing waterlines will be
installed along portions of the proposed roadway alignments as part of the project
construction These new waterlines will be 150 mm in diameter and will consist of PVC
pipes In addition we envision that water laterals 560 mm connecting the waterlines to
service the existing homes will be required In general the following guidelines may be
used for installation of the waterlines for the proposed roadway project
The stress distribution against the bottom of a PVC pipe has a significant effect on
the load supporting capacity of the pipe Therefore the pipe bedding is an important
design consideration For waterlines bearing on the in situ clayey silt soils a minimum of
150 mm of bedding material should be provided below the pipe The bedding may be
reduced to 100 mm for the water laterals 50 mm diameter For pipes with inverts near
the soft loose soils a stabilization layer consisting of 500 mm of drain rock wrapped in a
non woven geotextile should be provided below the bedding layer for more uniform
support The bedding material should consist of select granular material free from rocks
25 mm or larger in any dimension or free from rocks of such size as recommended by the
pipe manufacturer whichever is smaller In addition the granular bedding material should
be free draining and should not have more than 10 percent particles less than
In general the initial backfill should consist of select granular material similar to the
bedding layer extending up to at least 300 mm above the top of the pipes It is critical that
a free draining granular material be used to reduce the potential for formation of voids
below the haunches of pipes and to provide adequate support for the sides of the pipes
The initial backfill should be densified with the use of a vibratory plate or similar light
compaction equipment The use of on site clayey soils as initial backfill immediately
around pipes is not recommended
W O 3595 00 B ArOLABS HAWAII Page 114
SECTION VI DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS
The final backfill extending from 300 mm above the top of the pipes to the
pavement subgrades may consist of general fill material The backfill should be
moisture conditioned to above the optimum moisture content placed in level lifts on the
order of about 150 to 200 mm in loose thickness and compacted to at least 90 percent
relative compaction
Due to the proximity of the waterline pipe to the finished subgrades we recommend
that a minimum cover of 900 mm be maintained between the top of the waterline pipe and
the finished pavement grade for waterline pipes constructed within the pavement areas
The Contractor should exercise care when preparing the subgrade for the pavement
above a waterline trench to avoid crushing the PVC pipe from the weight of the
construction equipment
M Shoring
We understand that temporary excavations may be required for construction of
some of the drainage structures and possibly the bridge foundations Open cut
excavation may be desirable provided that the excavation may be setback away from
existing on grade and below grade structures and utility lines Based on the boring
information we believe that temporary cut slopes on the order of about or flatter
may be used for open cut excavations in the stiff saprolite soils anticipated at the project
site Temporary open cut excavations in the granular causeway fills may be made with
slopes of about or flatter Excavated soils should not be stockpiled closer than a
horizontal distance equal to the depth of the excavation from the edge of the excavation to
reduce the potential for ground movement
Open cut excavations greater than 2 meters deep in the soft and or loose alluvial
and mangrove swamp deposits are not recommended and should be shored Excavations
into the soft subsoils should be made only with proper shoring installation Therefore we
recommend that the excavations to construct the drainage structures in soft soils and to
remove the soft soils under the drainage structures be shored One possible shoring
method is to use a sheet pile shoring system It should be noted that the bottom of some
of these excavations may encounter dense volcanic breccia formation and would not
SECTION VI DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS
readily provide toe embedment for the sheet pile shoring Therefore other means of
providing the passive pressures needed at the toe of the sheet pile shoring such as a
tremie concrete plug or predrilling into the rock formation would be necessary Other
temporary shoring systems may also be considered
The excavation support and shoring system used must comply with all applicable
safety requirements and the adequacy and safety of the shoring installation should be
made the sole responsibility of the Contractor His her representative who should be
required to be continuously present on site during excavation and construction work will
have the best opportunity to promptly observe any changing conditions during
construction such as unforeseen subsoils unexpectedly high groundwater table
inappropriate construction sequence or techniques etc which may affect shoring stability
In general some minor movements of the shoring system and the adjacent ground
may still occur due to changes in earth stresses during excavation Due to the complexity
of the stress changes it is difficult to accurately estimate the magnitude of movement
The magnitude also depends greatly upon workmanship such as how quickly and tightly
the shoring and bracing supports are installed on the subsoil conditions the size of the
excavation and the rate of excavation Therefore it is important to realize that the
excavation shoring should be installed properly and as early as practical if necessary and
that the adjacent ground should be continuously monitored for cracks dips and or other
indications of movements with instruments It is recommended that a qualified
geotechnical engineer be retained by the Contractor to design and evaluate the shoring
system used
N Dewatering
Dewatering of some excavations will be necessary where the planned excavation
extends below the existing groundwater level Therefore we recommend that dewatering
provisions be included in the contract documents for construction Since the excavation
will involve discharge of groundwater a permit may be necessary The Contractor should
consult their independent consultant or the Republic of Palau Environmental Quality
SECTION VI DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS
Protection Board EQPB for the latest regulations and information pertaining to any
required permit application
Dewatering for construction is the responsibility of the Contractor The selection of
equipment and methods of dewatering should be left up to the Contractor and he she
should be aware that modifications to the dewatering system may be required during
construction depending on the conditions encountered The dewatering method selected
should have minimal impact on the groundwater level surrounding the proposed
excavation
It is our opinion that the definition of Dewatering in the contract documents should
be written to include all works or systems required to lower the natural groundwater table
and or to exclude the water from the excavations to allow construction of the proposed
structures under safe and dry conditions These works or systems may include but are
not limited to well pumping grouting cut off walls tremie concrete plugs or any
combination of the above and or other possible methods
1 Dewatering Considerations
We suggest that the following three basic criteria be considered in selection of a
suitable method of dewatering
e The dewatering method should result in the least disturbance or damage to
existing structures roads and environment
The dewatering method should maintain stability of and also provide safe
and dry working conditions in the excavation
9 The dewatering method should be sufficiently flexible to allow modifications
to accommodate various ground conditions
2 Dewatering Precaution and Monitoring
The potential impact of the dewatering system selected on depressing the natural
groundwater table must be carefully evaluated by the Contractor prior to
dewatering It is recommended that a qualified geotechnical engineer be retained
W O 3595 00 B GEOLAnS aA Page 117
SECTION VI DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS
by the Contractor to design and evaluate the dewatering system used The impact
and safety of the dewatering operations should be made the sole responsibility of
the Contractor His her qualified representative who should be required to be
continuously present on site during dewatering activities will have the best
opportunity to promptly observe the effects of dewatering during construction and to
implement as soon as possible necessary precautionary or remedial measures
including but not limited to stopping or slowing down the dewatering operations
Where encountered at the bottom of excavations permeable granular subsoils may
be susceptible to piping and quick conditions The dewatering operations should
be carried out without creating a quick condition or softening at the bottom of
excavation Therefore the project dewatering operations should be done without
pumping out soil fines pumping clear water only and should be coordinated with
shoring installation such that the excavation stability is not adversely affected
Excessive pumping which removes soil fines may result in a blowing or heaving
of the excavation bottom or sides
END OF DISCUSSION AND STRUCTURE RECOMMENDATIONS

A Design Review
It is recommended that preliminary and final drawings and specifications for the
proposed construction be forwarded to Geolabs Hawaii for review and written
comments prior to advertisement for bids This review is necessary to evaluate
conformance of the plans and specifications with the intent of the foundation and
earthwork recommendations provided herein If this review is not made
Geolabs Hawaii cannot assume responsibility for misinterpretation of our
recommendations
B Construction Observation
It is recommended that Geolabs Hawaii be retained to provide geotechnical
engineering services during the construction of this project The items of construction
monitoring that are critical requiring Special Inspection include the following
Removal of soft and or loose soils
Soft soil stabilization measures
Subgrade preparation
Fill placement and compaction testing
Review of settlement data
Review of shoring and dewatering submittals
Observation of foundation excavations
Observation of drilled shaft foundation installation and
Observation of test pile and production pile installation
Other aspects of earthwork construction should also be observed by a
representative from Geolabs Hawaii This is to observe compliance with the design
concepts specifications or recommendations and to expedite suggestions for design
changes that may be required in the event that subsurface conditions differ from those
anticipated at the time this report was prepared Geolabs Hawaii should be accorded the
opportunity to provide construction observation services to confirm the assumptions made
in formulating the recommendations presented in this report
W O 3595 00 B Page 119
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION VII POST DESIGN SERVICES SERVICES DURING CONSTRUCTION
If the actual exposed subsurface conditions encountered during construction differ
from those assumed or considered in this report Geolabs Hawaii should be contacted to
review and or revise the geotechnical engineering recommendations presented herein
Any import fill material required should be tested for conformance with the project
specifications prior to hauling to the project site
We understand that Geolabs Hawaii may not be retained to provide on site
construction observation during the foundation and earthwork operations due to the locality
of the project site from our office We understand that a Contractor Quality Control CQC
representative will be used for the project He she should be experienced in
construction observation and testing of earthwork operations and foundation installations
The following minimum requirements should be used to select CQC representatives
1 CQC Representative
The CQC Representative shall be a graduate engineer or a graduate of an
equivalent construction oriented college program with a minimum of five years
construction experience on similar type construction to this project including at
least two years of experience in quality control
2 Alternate CQC Representative
As part of the CQC staff the Contractor shall designate an alternate to act for the
CQC Representative in the event that the CQC Representative is absent from
the construction site The alternate may not act for the CQC Representative for a
period longer than 30 consecutive calendar days The alternate
CQC Representative shall either be a graduate engineer or a graduate of an
equivalent construction oriented college program with a minimum one year of
quality control experience or a person with a minimum three years of
construction experience on similar type construction to the project and including
at least one year of quality control experience

SECTION VIII LIMITATIONS
The findings analyses and recommendations submitted in this report are based
upon the information obtained through our literature research past project experience
site reconnaissance and field exploration performed for the proposed Palau Compact
Road Package B project Variations of conditions between and beyond the field
borings are likely to occur considering the long linear feature of the roadway alignment
Therefore the nature and extent of these variations may not become evident until
construction is underway If variations then appear evident it will be necessary to
reevaluate the findings and recommendations provided in this report
The locations of the field borings indicated in this report are approximate having
been estimated from the survey stakes placed along the alignment by R M Towill
Corporation and by taping from reference points and visible features shown on the
Preliminary Road Alignment Plans dated January 1997 and Plans for Construction of a
Portion of Palau Compact Road Package B dated prepared by
Earth Tech The maps were used in conjunction with field compass readings distance
relationships from known features topography altimeter and Global Positioning System
equipment to obtain the approximate boring locations as shown on the Site Plans
Elevations of the borings were estimated from the contour lines shown on the same plans
borings should be considered accurate only to the degree implied by the methods used
The stratification breaks shown on the graphic representations of the borings depict
the approximate boundaries between soil rock types and as such may denote a gradual
transition Water level data from the borings were measured at the times shown on the
graphic representations and or presented in the text of this report These data have been
reviewed and interpretations made in the formulation of this report However it must be
noted that fluctuation may occur due to variation in rainfall tidal fluctuation time of year
temperature and other factors
W O 3595 00 B Page 121
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION VIII LIMITATIONS
This report has been prepared for the exclusive use of Earth Tech their Client the
U S Army Corps of Engineers and other design subconsultants for specific application to
Package B of the proposed Palau Compact Road project in accordance with generally
accepted geotechnical engineering principles and practices No warranty is expressed or
implied
This report has been prepared solely for the purpose of assisting the design
engineers in the design evaluation of the proposed project Therefore this report may not
contain sufficient data or the proper information to serve as the basis for preparation of
construction cost estimates or contract bidding A Contractor wishing to bid on this project
should retain a competent geotechnical engineer to assist in the interpretation of this
report and or in the performance of additional site specific exploration for bid estimating
purposes
The Owner Client should be aware that unanticipated soil conditions are commonly
encountered Unforeseen soil conditions such as perched groundwater soft loose
deposits and hard layers or cavities may occur in localized areas and may require
additional probing or corrections in the field which may result in construction delays to
attain a properly constructed project Therefore a sufficient contingency fund is
recommended to accommodate these possible extra costs

CONSTRUCTION PROCEDURES FOR STAGE CONSTRUCTION
Subgrade Preparation
Clear existing ground surface of vegetation debris and deleterious materials
Soft Ground Stabilization
Place woven geotextile or geogrid as appropriate
Place 0 75 m minimum thickness granular fill or surge rock fill layer as appropriate
For layers greater than 1 m thick place additional geogrids at 0 5 m height intervals
Settlement Gauge and Piezometer Installation
Install settlement gauges and vibrating wire piezometers
Take two baseline readings one day min 24 hours apart 10 days prior to site filling
Take readings on a weekly basis during entire settlement monitoring program
Note Readings of the vibrating wire piezometers are taken near continuously using data loggers
Download data and
Stage 1 Fill Placement Requirements
Place fill at a rate of not more than 1 m per week up to a maximum of 5 m including stabilization layer
Extend settlement gauges as necessary during fill placement
Establish settlement markers at the top of the Stage 1 fill embankment
Allow fill to settle during settlement waiting period for Stage 1 approximately 4 to 6 months
Monitor settlement gauges settlement markers and piezometers on a weekly basis
during entire embankment construction and settlement monitoring period
Proceed with Stage 2 if additional fill required wnen 70 to 80 percent of pore pressure build up in the
soft soils has dissipated
Stage 2 Fill Placement Requirements
Place fill at a rate of not more than 1 m per week up to a maximum of 8 m above the top elevation of Stage 1
Extend settlement gauges as necessary during fill placement
Establish settlement markers at the top of the Stage 2 fill embankment
Allow fill to settle during settlement waiting period for Stage 2 approximately 1 to 6 months
Monitor settlement gauges settlement markers and piezometers on a weekly basis
during entire embankment construction and settlement monitoring period
Proceed with Stage 3 if additional fill required when 70 to 80 percent of pore pressure build up in the
soft soils has disipated
Stage 3 Fill Placement Requirements
Place fill at a rate of not more than 1 m per week up to a maximum of 11 m above the top elevation of Stage 2
Extend settlement gauges as necessary during fill placement
Establish settlement markers at the top of Stage 3 fill embankment
Allow fill to settle during settlement waiting period for Stage 3 approximately 1 to 3 months
Monitor settlement gauges settlement markers and piezometers on a weekly basis
during entire embankment construction and settlement monitoring period
Fine Grading and Pavement Construction
Proceed with fine grading when settlements reach near equilibrium
Proceed with pavement construction when settlements reach equilibrium
Areas designated as Stage Construction shall commence as early as possible to allow
the soft soils to consolidate under the fill loads

APPENDIX A
Field Exploration
APPENDIX A
Field Exploration
The subsurface conditions along the proposed roadway alignment for Package B of
the proposed Palau Compact Road project were explored by drilling and sampling
38 borings designated as Boring Nos B 201 through B 237 including B 235A The
borings extended to depths ranging from about 1 0 to 42 8 meters below the existing
ground surface using hand auger and various drill rigs equipped with continuous flight
augers and coring tools The field exploration was conducted from May 29 1997 through
In addition a supplemental field exploration was undertaken from
April 28 through May 13 1998 to explore the realigned portion of the roadway The
shown on the Site Plans Plates 3 1 through 3 3
The materials encountered in the borings were classified by visual and textural
examination in the field by an engineer and or a geologist who monitored the drilling
operations on a near continuous basis These classifications were further reviewed
visually and by testing in the laboratory Soils were classified in general conformance with
the Unified Soil Classification System as shown on Plate A Graphic representations of
the materials encountered are presented on the Logs of Borings Plates A 1 1 through
A 38 1
Soil samples were obtained from the drilled borings in general accordance with
ASTM Test Designation D 1586 84 Penetration Test and Split Barrel Sampling of Soils
by driving a 50 mm OD standard penetration sampler or a 75 mm OD Modified California
sampler with a 63 5 kilogram hammer falling 760 millimeters The blow counts needed to
drive the sampler the last 300 mm of a 450 mm drive are shown on the Logs of Borings at
the appropriate sample depths
Pocket penetrometer and torvane shear tests were performed on selected cohesive
soil samples retrieved in the field The pocket penetrometer test provides an indication of
the unconfined compressive strength of the soil sample The torvane shear test provides
a quick estimate of the undrained shear strength of the soil sample Results of the pocket
are presented on the Logs of Borings at the appropriate sample depths
Core samples of the dense breccia and hard tuff rock formations encountered at
the site were obtained using diamond core drilling techniques in general accordance with
ASTM Standard Practice D 2113 83 Diamond Core Drilling for Site Investigation Core
drilling is a rotary drilling method which uses a hollow bit to cut into the rock formation
The material left in the hollow core of the bit is mechanically recovered for examination
and description
GEOLABS HAWAII
APPENDIX A FIELD EXPLORATION
Recovery REC is used as a subjective guide to the interpretation of the relative
quality of rock masses Recovery is defined as the actual length of material recovered
from a coring attempt versus the length of the core attempt such as if 1200 mm of material
is recovered from a 1500 mm core run the recovery would be 80 percent and would be
shown on the Logs of Borings as REC 80
The Rock Quality Designation RQD is also a subjective guide to the relative
quality of rock masses RQD is defined as the percentage of the core run that is sound
material in excess of 100 mm in length without any discontinuities discounting any
drilling induced fractures or breaks If 750 mm of sound material is recovered from a
1500 mm core run the RQD would be 50 percent and would be shown on the Logs of
Borings as RQD 50 Generally the following is used to describe the relative quality of
the rock based on the Practical Handbook of Physical Properties of Rocks and Minerals
Rock Quality RQD
The rippability of a rock mass is a function of the relative hardness of the rock its
relative quality brittleness and fissile characteristics A dense rock formation with a high
RQD would be very difficult to rip and would probably require more arduous methods of
excavation
Twenty three bulk samples designated as Sample Nos S 201 through S 223 of
the near surface soils were obtained at selected locations along the roadway alignment
The bulk samples were generally collected from the proposed cut locations to evaluate the
materials for use as embankment fills The approximate locations of the near surface bulk
samples are summarized in Table A 2 and are shown on the Site Plans Plates 3 1
through 3 3

Geology Soils and Foundation Engineering ISLAND OF BABELDAOB REPUBLIC OF PALAU
APPENDIX B
Laboratory Testing
APPENDIX B
Laboratory Testing
Samples recovered from our field exploration program performed for Package B of
the proposed Palau Compact Road project were visually examined and classified in our
laboratories in Babeldaob Palau and Honolulu Hawaii Selected samples were tested to
evaluate the physical characteristics and engineering properties of the soils encountered
The laboratory testing program was formulated with the emphasis on evaluating the
moisture density plasticity gradation compressibility shear strength and compaction
characteristics of the soils encountered
The laboratory tests performed included determination of dry density and natural
moisture content Atterberg Limits sieve analysis hydrometer unconfined compression
triaxial compression direct shear consolidation modified consolidation collapse
potential Modified Proctor compaction California Bearing Ratio CBR and corrosion
are presented on Plates B 1 through B 80 of Appendix B Detailed descriptions of the
various tests performed for this exploration are presented below
Moisture and Density
Moisture content and dry density tests were performed on selected soil samples to
aid in defining the interface between the various soil layers encountered and correlating
the layers between test borings The moisture content tests were performed in general
accordance with ASTM Test Designation D 2216 The results of these tests are
the appropriate sample depths
Atterberg Limits
Seventeen Atterberg Limits tests were performed on selected soil samples to
evaluate the liquid limit LL plastic limit PL and plasticity index Pl as an aid in
classifying the soils The Atterberg Limits tests were performed in general accordance
with ASTM Test Designation D 4318 The test results are summarized on the Logs of
presentations of the test results are provided on Plates B 1 and B 2
Sieve Analysis and Hydrometer
To provide information on the particle size distribution of the soils encountered
twenty five sieve analysis tests including twenty two hydrometer tests were performed to
evaluate the gradation characteristics and to aid in soil classification The tests were
performed in accordance with ASTM Test Designation C 136 and D422 Graphic
presentations of the test results are provided on Plates B 3 through B 7
APPENDIX B LABORATORY TESTING
Unconfined Compression
To evaluate the unconfined compressive strength of the on site clayey soils four
unconfined compression tests were performed on selected in situ samples in accordance
with ASTM Test Designation D 2166 The test results are shown on the Logs of Borings at
the appropriate sample depths and summarized on Table B 2 Individual stress strain
curves of the unconfined compression tests are presented on Plates B 8 through B 11
Unconsolidated Undrained Triaxial Compression
To evaluate the undrained shear strength of the clayey soils ten unconsolidated
undrained triaxial compression tests were performed on selected in situ and remolded soil
samples in accordance with ASTM Test Designation D 2850 The approximate in situ
effective overburden pressure was used as the applied confining pressure for the
undisturbed samples For the remolded samples the confining pressure was varied to
reflect different fill heights up to about 20 meters thick The test results and the
stress strain curves are presented on Plates B 12 through B 21
Multi Stage Triaxial Consolidated Undrained Compression Test
To evaluate the long term shear strengths of the clayey soils when used as fill
embankment one consolidated undrained triaxial compression test was performed on a
remolded soil sample in accordance with ASTM Test Designation D 4767 The test results
Direct Shear
To evaluate the shear strength characteristics of the in situ soils and remolded soils
as fill materials seventeen strained controlled consolidated drained direct shear tests
were performed on the in situ and remolded soil samples in accordance with ASTM Test
Designation D 3080 The test results are presented on Plates B 22 through B 39
Consolidation
Nine consolidation tests were performed on selected soil samples to evaluate the
compressibility characteristics of the on site soils These tests were performed in
accordance with ASTM Test Designation D 2435 and the test results are plotted on Plates
B 40 through B 48
Modified Consolidation Collapse Potential
The conventional consolidation tests were modified to evaluate the compressibility
characteristics of the remolded soil samples under different surcharge pressures A soil
sample is remolded at its natural moisture content to approximately 85 percent relative
compaction to simulate the anticipated field conditions The remolded soil sample is
allowed to settle until it has stabilized under a surcharge load Water is then added to the
APPENDIX B LABORATORY TESTING
soil sample to evaluate its collapse or swell potential in a saturated condition Two sets of
modified consolidation tests were performed and the test results are presented on Plates
B 49 and B 50
Modified Proctor Test
Fourteen laboratory compaction tests were performed on the bulk samples
obtained to evaluate the relationship between the moisture content and the dry density of
the near surface soils The Modified Proctor tests were performed in accordance with
ASTM Test Designation D 1557 using the moist preparation method wet to dry The test
results are summarized in Table B 3 and are graphically presented on Plates B 51 through
B 64
California Bearing Ratio CBR
Seventeen CBR tests were performed on the near surface soils to evaluate the
strength of the in situ cohesive materials for pavement support The tests were performed
in accordance with ASTM Test Designation D 1883 near the natural moisture content
The test results are summarized in Table B 3 and are presented on Plates B 65 through
B 79
Corrosion Test
One set of minimum resistivity ASTM G57 chloride
and sulfate tests was performed on a selected soil sample obtained from our
field exploration The test results are presented on Plate B 80

From Troy A Ogasawara
Re Palau Compact Road Soil Analysis Report
To follow is a brief summary and recommendations for the attached soil test report no 863 011
from the Palau Compact Road Project
Results
The soil pH is acidic between 04 This is very typical of highly leached or weathered
soils In most cases a pH between is desirable At pH ranges below 5 5 Aluminum
toxicity may inhibit adequate vegetation
The phosphate P levels are extremely low This nutrient is always critical to initial grow in and
establishment of any crop Most native tropical soils are naturally low in this element In
general phosphate is a nutrient which should be incorporated in the root zone prior to planting
Potassium K could become limiting and should be applied during the initial pre plant and
maintenance periods Potassium sulfate would be a better source of this element rather than
potassium chloride The potassium chloride is much more soluble as compared to the sulfate
form and will be easily leached out of the effective root zone
The calcium Ca levels are extremely low and will severely restrict growth and establishment on
most crops The low pH of these soils are related to the low levels of calcium
The magnesium Mg levels are slightly low As the other bases K Ca are increased
moderate amounts of magnesium should be applied to prevent this element from becoming
deficient
Hydrogen H expressed as a percent of the base saturation is extremely high This is an
indication the the soil is acidic As calcium carbonate or other liming material is added the
hydrogen levels will decrease
Sodium levels are low and should not pose any problem in the establishment of most crops
The excessive quantities of aluminum Al are within the toxic ranges Aluminum toxicity is quite
common on highly leached tropical sub soils High levels of available aluminum will inhibit plant
growth and or severely reduce the rate of establishment As soil pH calcium levels and
phosphate levels are increased the amounts of available aluminum will decrease However given
the extremely poor nutritive status of these soils large amounts of both elements calcium and
phosphate must be applied
Recommendations
In most situations a pre plant amendment program will recommend the phosphate and liming
materials be thoroughly incorporated into the soil profile to a depth of 8 15 centimeters
However given the steepness of the slopes and potential increased threat of erosion and the
proximity to the roadway incorporation may not be practical Additions of large quantities of
lime could potentially cause damage i e burning of the delicate seedling roots Again most
typical liming recommendations will advise the incorporation into the root zone to reduce the
burn potential and allow for pH modification of the profile
Due to its low solubility and other interactions with the soil lime applied topically will produce
little short term effects lower in the profile Additions of large quantities of gypsum will
produce slight pH increases on severely acidic soils Being many times more soluble than lime
up to 150 times gypsum when topically applied will be able to move through the soil profile
Therefore a combination of gypsum and lime would be a practical approach to this situation
I would recommend the following pre plant amendments be applied during the hydromulching
non incorporated operation
Kilograms Hectare Finely Ground Dolomitic Limestone
Kilograms Hectare Agricultural Grade Gypsum Calcium Sulfate
Maintenance applications should consist of a high phosphate complete analysis fertilizer and
finely ground dolomitic lime stone This material should be applied approximately 6 weeks after
planting and seed germination
Kilograms Hectare Finely Ground Dolomitic Limestone
If incorporation of pre plant soil amendments is possible the dolomitic lime stone rates should
be increased to 4 480 kilograms per hectare and thoroughly incorporated along with the pre plant
fertilizer into the effective root zone of The maintenance application of dolomite
could then be removed
Other options which should be considered are
1 Topically applied pre treatment of the slopes with a hydraulically applied slurry of
hydrated lime several weeks prior to installing the non incorporated pre plant soil
amendments
2 Installation of aluminum tolerant plants
3 Application of pre plant amendments prior to sheep foot rolling tracking the soil surface
with a dozer and light scarification which will create a mixing into the soil profile
These soils if properly treated should be able to sustain adequate vegetation required for erosion
control
If you have any questions please give me a call
